<Rate>5</Rate>< text>
This review is only based on the strawberry croissant and service.

Parking is easy with the big lot. The line starts close to the front door and service is quick. 1 strawberry croissant is $1.70 and get 6 for $10.20. They have sandwiches in the fridge to the left and other baked goods in the line walkway. All cakes and curry rice must be preordered the day before? I think.

The strawberry croissant was crispy and not super sweet. The flaky croissant to custard to strawberry ratio was just right so it's light and fresh.<//text>

< Text>
an absolutely adorable location. lots of space, beautiful lighting, and great food selection. i love the inclusion of savory foods because as phenomenal as their pastries are, especially the strawberry croissants, sometimes i just want a warm savory dish. i took my grandpa here on a rainy day, and we split their small tray of chicken katsu curry. the rice was perfectly cooked, the chicken was crispy but not dry, and the curry sauce was perfectly seasoned. the staff is always polite as well, whether im just picking up a few croissants or settling down for a meal.<//Text>

<date>1605633082097< /date>< review>
I already reviewed the original location in Tustin years ago so don't have a whole lot to say in terms of pastries, as they taste the same.  However, I do like this new location because it's huge and much less crowded than the Tustin location.  It's in a standalone location with no other businesses so you don't have to compete for parking spots with other stores.

I rarely got anything other than its famous strawberry croissants at the Tustin location but decided to also get Azuki Cream and Cream Pan.  Given the name of this place is Cream Pan, I'm surprised I never tried one before.  To be honest, it was just ok.  It's basically bread filled with custard cream.  Strawberry croissants were excellent, as usual.  Azuki Cream was really good too.  It's pastry filled with sweet red beans and cream.  This item may become one of my regular items to purchase here.

Face mask is required for entry and is following social distance guidelines, although not sure how much they are enforcing it. There's a hand sanitizer by the entrance as well.</review>

<username>Jessica Labidi< /username><Time>1384811751963< /Time><Rate>1</Rate>< review>
This is the very first apartment that my husband and I lived in, we thought when we moved in we were getting a good deal with their move in special.  The time we lived here was from November 2012 to October 2013. However, after a few months of living here we noticed all over our apartment there was mold growing; from our bathroom to the windows in our bedroom, kitchen, even on our refrigerator.  A month after we had moved in the Manager at the time had mentioned to me one evening that if we had seen any mold to let her know immediately, at that time I did not because we had just moved in and they had cleaned and covered it before we moved in.  So when we started to see mold growing I went straight to the office Manager, but at this point the Manager before had already left, and a new one had come in to replace her.  The new management was very unprofessional and did not take our issue seriously, she walked over to our place took a look around and said she would get maintenance to come and paint over what was coming through the walls.  This did not solve our issue, and on top of this my husband and I started to suffer from allergies from the mold, and my husband started to develop asthma attacks, especially at night, we both had difficulties sleeping in the apartment.  We complained again, and once again Management ignored our complaints, telling us that is was the weather changing even though this lasted for almost a year, and they told us to spray bleach on our walls.  Finally when our lease was up, we were ready to move, we could not wait to get out of this horrible place.  They made it appear like a decent place to live, but on the inside, it is miserable, do not sign a lease with ARNEL Management.  On top of this when we moved in we paid $650 for our deposit and they basically take it all when you move out, and we cleaned the apartment the best we could before we left.  Once my husband and I moved out, after a week a not breathing in that apartment my husband no longer was sneezing every day, coughing at night, having shortness of breathes and having asthma attacks, so I know it was not the weather, but the mold in the apartment.  When we moved out the maintenance had told us that the carpet had been in that apartment for 7 years, and every year they just paint over everything, and the appliances had not been upgraded for more than at least 10 years.  Cinnamon Creek and Arnel Properties are a joke, and should be shut down because the living conditions that are life threatening.</review>

I've been banking with SESLOC for 10+ years, and had excellent service. We've opened multiple accounts, including several for our kids, made many wire transfers & inter-account transfers, no problems.

When it comes down to it, the biggest reason to choose a local credit union is this: SESLOC isn't trying to suck your money out and funnel it to corporate shareholders like major commercial banks; they're locally run, and they're a credit union, meaning that *you* are the shareholders. < Review>
In my experience, SESLOC customer service has greatly declined in the past five years.  Increasingly, they have gotten more difficult to access - closing branches that were close to us and opening up in other areas that are not at all convenient - at least to us.  They have started to institute banking policies that are inconvenient and impersonal - for example, refusing to let me transfer money from savings to checking on line, because I was only allowed to do make six online transfers in one month (they never told me this before and the first five transfers were automatic transfers that they had initiated - not me!).  I was trying to make the online transfer to make sure I had sufficient funds to cover a check - and I had to drive all the way down to their very inconvenient office (a half hour from my home) to make the transfer in person. Their new branch office is ugly, poorly planned, wasteful of space, and very impersonal.  I have transferred my banking to US Bank, which despite being a very large bank, is so much more personal than SESLOC.  So sorry to see a credit union we have used for over 15 years become such an impersonal, bureaucratic nightmare.< /Review>

<review>I have tried many different Thai restaurants around the bay area and Champa has the best pad thai to my opinion. It is very flavorful and it is not too sweet like some other restaurants. I love all of the noodle dishes, but the only down side is that the meats (beef specifically) are generally rough and hard to chew. I like the curry dishes as well. Although the sampler is one of their most popular dishes, the crispy rice is not crispy enough to me. One thing that I notice is that during Covid time, the food quality went down by a little. It is still good, but not as good as before.</review>< pics>

I want to have big neighborhood pride but I just find Champa Garden too frustrating to do business with anymore.  They've never had adequate phone equipment to be able to hear orders.  The website died 2-3 years ago and they couldn't be bothered to fix it -- third party sites have old versions of the menu.  Sometimes they don't answer the phone. Champa Garden has definitely become our new dinner spot. They serve up tasty Lao and Thai dishes  that will make you continue to salivate long after your should've stopped eating. We like to take friends, order a few dishes, and serve it up family style.

Heads up they're pretty strict about closing on time so don't be upset if you show up half an hour before closing and they won't seat you. Also, expect to wait up to an hour if you show up at peak dinner time. This place gets packed. But in my experience, once you've been seated everything goes by pretty quick!

Minus one star for serving the Thai iced tea in single use platic cups when we were dining in, sorry.<//Text>

<userid>104287900749560866993< /userid><name>Yvette Ngo< /name><Time>1386733473115</Time><rate>4< /rate>< Text>
This place is a very casual Laotian restaurant.  Don't expect the best customer service. The cuisine is a cross between Vietnamese and Thai food. I ordered the crispy rice appetizer and it was delicious! The chopped scallions really added a lot to the dish as well as the lettuce wraps. The whole dish tasted fresh and well-balanced with all the greens, since it is a fried dish. The pad see ew was okay. I've had better elsewhere. The panang curry was delicious. Make sure to ask for the condiment tray (huge tray with spices and sauces) to make your dishes more spicy. The best part was that the bill came out to $24 for two people. Amazing!< /Text>

<user_id>116649869062956301765</user_id>< review>
The service I just received was nothing less than atrotious.

I ordered chicken pad Thai, sticky rice and Thom Ka soup for takes-out at 5:06. At 5:55 my meal still hadn't arrived. I watched my friend get served within 15 minutes-  and she came 15 minutes after me and she was treated well and with courtesy. It was 5:35.

I thought nothing of it, so I sat and waited. 5:40.

Three people walked in after me, ordered for pick up and got served. They came at various times-5:30ish, 5:20 ish, 5:40 or so, and got served.

That's not the end of it. Not yet.  I counted three or more tables with more than three people to each table who also came after I ordered get, you guessed it, served.

Now mind you I'm sitting right in front of the table where the cashier is located and where they place all the orders. They would look at me waiting, waiting and waiting without informing me about the status of my meal and why it's so late. They didn't have the courtesy to speak to me and would pretend they were too busy for me.

They ignored me and politely smiled and asked each new person coming in " may I help you sir? How many people in your party?
I'm clearing the table right now for your party" and withing less than a minute they were seated. 15 to twenty minutes, served. I continued to wait.

I'm one person who ordered three items for take out who sat right in front of the servers, waiters, cashier,  etc. And not only was I ignored, but when they finally talked to me they blamed the person who took my order and said " something is wrong with the cashier machine and paper" huh!? But yet everyone else around me got their orders with no "cashier machine is broke" excuses. No, they got served and I got excuses and still waited. Waited. Then I cancelled my meal and had to wait while they processed my card and return my funds , that took an additional 10 to 15 minutes for them to do that, and I still f#&$'3&* waited.

So, after an hour later, they processed my refund and still I waited because they forgot to inform me that my debit card was credited back to my funds!

So, what did I get for this piss poor service? A free chicken pad Thai!

I have never wrote such a scorching review of any restaurant. Never. Ever. But this was the last straw. I've lived in this neighborhood for years. I ate in this restaurant, told my friends about it and was even proud of the quality of the food at the best prices around.  But not anymore.

Things have gotten worse, much worse, within the past 4 years or so which I assume is due to getting more popular and more growth. With this have come growing pains and I believe they don't have the right infrastructure and resources to adequately serve them all.

I would order from them on many occasions in the past and I noticed my wait time increasing each time and tonight was the last straw.

I was one of your loyal customers, but not anymore. I will tell my friends about you, I will  post this review to other websites and  I will not patronize your establishment again.</review>

< Text>
What a hidden gem!

I wasn't able to order the sampler (which is their most popular dish) because I don't eat meat. But I tried the egg rolls and they're my favorite that I've had! They have a different wrapping, and eating wrapped with the lettuce then dipping it in fish sauce was delicious.

Laos larb was an interesting dish. The duck curry, garlic shrimp, and thai tea are all good! I ordered the pad kee mao the first time I came, and it was really bland. So avoid this dish if you can and try and order their specials.

Come during an off time so you don't have to wait!

Tip: There's websites that have coupons which make dining here even more affordable!< /Text>

< review>
Frenzied little Laotian/Thai/Lue joint on a random residential corner in East Oakland.

Champa Garden hasn't done what most ethnic restaurants do: tone down the flavors to not offend. The papaya salad (get it Lao style!) packs a wallop. As Padma says, sometimes you just want to get hit in the face with shrimp paste.

Definitely not a flavor that'll please most, but if you can get past all the waves of pungent and fermented seafood, there's a lot to marvel at before the spiciness slams you in the aftertaste.

The Lue noodle soup was great. Big wide rice noodles in a red pork broth, plenty of fragrant oil floating about.

Definitely get the rice ball salad to start, and the catfish dish was rocking as well. Big chunks of fish in a curry sauce, with lots of veggies to round it out.<//review>

< username>
Catherine Chang< /username>
<Text>This place is a flavor bomb!!!! The Champa Sample is a must-order. It includes Laos spicy sausages, vermicelli noodles, mushroom + silver noodle egg rolls, and fried rice ball salad with fish sauce on the side! I love ordering the most exotic sounding dishes on the menu when I try out a new cuisine (I've never had Laos before, but the flavor palette seems close to Vietnamese and Thai). Naturally, the fried rice ball salad caught my eye. What on earth is a fried rice ball salad?! It's crispy goodness, including fried rice (OMG A SALAD WITH CARBS?! HELL YES!) mixed with preserved pork, green onions, peanuts, cilantro, mint leaves, and lime juice.

We also got the angel wings, which can be best described as a spring roll wrapped inside a deboned chicken drumstick. Drizzle some of that sweet and sour sauce on top and you got a ticket straight to deep fried heaven!

The mango fried rice was also delightful. My boyfriend is usually staunchly a noodle guy, but even he caved to this magical dish. The Laos-style beef larb was not as pungent and flavorful as I would have hoped, but it was still delicious.

Service and atmosphere was mediocore. The staff seemed on the unfriendly and on the shy side, but nothing horrible. For such a cozy establishment, I think it goes a long way for customers to be greeted with a big smile and at least some level of enthusiasm. Sadly, I felt like my excitement over the food and the menu was not shared by the host or our waitress.<//Text><time>1418673310323</time>< resp>
None<//resp>
